I love the iPhone 15 pro. The 15 plus is great - massive battery life  and light in the hand compared to the 15 pro max.  However, the 15 pro is easier to hold. Audio quality is up compared to the iPhone 14 for wired, wireless and speakers. The action button is brilliant. I configured mine to launch a different menu depending on focus mode (if you're not using focus modes and ios workflow shortcuts you really aren't getting the versatility and integrated customisation that is better than my android phones).  Camera and video are excellent on the 15 pro.  And os and security updates that will last 7 years with the phone, (based on past proven experience) lasting that long and still being performant.  For per year value the 15 series is hard to beat.  If you really want the best battery life gp for the 15 pro max or Sony 1vi, both of which lasted a lot longer than my Samsung ultra. The aony is narrower amd easier to hold than the 15 pro max and Samsung Ultra; it has a 3.5mm headphone socket and SD card slot. And the Sony 1vi camera, using raw, with its natural look compared to the sharpening with the Ultra outs the joy back into photography. However, the Sony 1vi only gets 4 years of security updates. But is leagues ahead of the ultra and 15 pro max for wireless audio, including newer Bluetooth and WiFi support.

The evolution of smartphone notches has been quite interesting over the years. iPhones introduced the concept of notches, setting a trend that Android devices quickly followed. However, Android took it a step further, refining the design by making the notches smaller and introducing innovative variations like the tear-drop notch and punch-hole camera displays. Interestingly, Apple chose not to directly copy Android's advancements and stuck with their notch design for a while. To cover up, they introduced a feature that some critics argue was more of a gimmick than an innovation: the "dynamic island," which, when you think about it, is essentially a stretched-out pattern resembling a punch-hole camera. iphone never want to accept defeat and come up with bullshit stuff to keeps the fools occupied for a couple of years, literally any android phone can have a dynamic island anywhere on their screen ğŸ˜‚

Everyone talks about the USBC port as an upgrade Apple decided to do, it was not. The EU passed a law that required all phones to use the port to make cables universal. So Apple had no choice.  The EU has also passed a law that goes in effect in a couple years requiring the ability for the customer to easily change batteries.   Regardless, all speculation about future no port phones is moot, the EU law requires it so it is here to stay and Apple is not happy about it. They fought the law hard but lost.
The only two big differences I see between the iPhone 14 and 15 is that Apple fixed the bad heat management of the iPhone 14, and switched from the archaic lightning port to an USB-C port - without using the speed advantages brought by the latter. The remaining changes are a number of incremental improvements which, in a pragmatic way, do not justify a Â£1000+ expense...

As an example for RE Village that you used, sure the resolution is 720p, but I think you didn't mention the fact that the PPI is very important. You won't notice the fact that it is only 720p as the pixel density of the phone screen is massive. I did the math, on a 32 inch screen running at the 1600x900 the PS4 would run at, you'd have a pixel density of 57.37. Now for the Iphone pro max having a display size of 6.7 Inch, the PPI is 219.2! That's incredible... So it will look incredibly sharp on such a small display. For reference, a 4k image of 3840 x 2160 on a 32 inch display is still 137.68 PPI... Which is still less than the Iphone 15 pro running at 720p... absolutely wild...
